Rational Proof for God's Hearing, Sight, and Speech
Sanusi presents a rational deduction that God must possess hearing, sight, and speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument that God must possess hearing, sight, and speech.

Core Idea
God's perfections are rationally necessary—absence would mean defect.

Sanusi now turns to a rational proof for three divine attributes: hearing, sight, and speech. While revelation confirms these attributes, reason alone can demonstrate their necessity. This lesson presents the logical argument that every living being must either have an attribute or its opposite, and since opposites are defects, God must possess the perfections.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Sanusi uses a very compressed style here.
2
Identify the key premise
The proof begins with the principle that every living being capable of an attribute is either not devoid of it, its like, or its opposite. Understand this foundational rule.
3
Follow the logical deduction
Trace the argument: living beings accept these three attributes (hearing, sight, speech) because dead beings cannot. This leads to the necessity that every living being must have them or face having their opposites.
The opposites are deafness, blindness, and muteness.
4
Understand why opposites are impossible for God
Sanusi argues that opposites are defects, and God is free from defects by consensus. Therefore, God must have the perfections.
This shows the rational necessity of these attributes.
5
Appreciate the role of reason
Note that this proof is rational, but Sanusi also mentions that transmitted evidence (revelation) is stronger. The lesson is that both reason and revelation affirm these attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ويدلُّ على اتِّصافِهِ تعالى بهذهِ الثلاثة : العقل . . . ) إلى آخره ؛ يعني : أَنَّهُ يُستدَلُّ على ثبوتِ هذه الصفات الثلاث ـ وهي السمع والبصر والكلام - بالعقل ، والسمع وهو أولى. أما وجه الاستدلال عليها بالعقل : فهو أَنَّ كلَّ حيّ قابل لصفةٍ فَإِنَّهُ لا يخلو عنها أو عن مثلها أو عن ضدّها ، ولما وجدنا الحيَّ هو الذي يقبلُ الاتصاف بهذه الصفاتِ الثلاث ؛ بدليل امتناع اتصاف الميتِ بها .. وجبَ أنْ يكونَ المُصرِّحُ لقبولِها : إمَّا الحياةَ وإما أمراً يلازم الحياة ، وأياً ما كانَ يلزمُ عليهِ قبولُ اتِّصافِ كل حي بها ، فإذا لم يتّصف بها الحيُّ لزمَ أن يتّصفَ بأضدادِها ؛ وهي الصَّمَمُ والعمى والبَكَمُ ، للكنَّ هذهِ الأضداد في حقّهِ تعالى مستحيلة ؛ لكونها آفاتِ ونقائص ، وهو جلَّ وعزَّ مُنزَّه عنها بإجماع العقلاء ، فوجب أن يتّصفَ تعالى بتلك الكمالات
His saying: 'And reason indicates His—may He be exalted—being described with these three...' to the end; that is: that the intellect is used to deduce the establishment of these three attributes—namely hearing, sight, and speech—and the transmitted evidence (al-sam‘) is more appropriate. As for the aspect of deduction by reason for them: it is that every living being capable of an attribute is either not devoid of it, or of its like, or of its opposite. And since we find that the living being is that which accepts being described with these three attributes—by the evidence of the impossibility of the dead being described with them—it is necessary that that which declares its acceptance is either life or something concomitant with life. And whichever it is, it necessitates the acceptance of the description of every living being with them. So if the living being is not described with them, it necessarily follows that it be described with their opposites, which are deafness, blindness, and muteness. But these opposites are impossible in the case of Him—may He be exalted—because they are defects and imperfections, and He—mighty and majestic—is exalted above them by the consensus of the rational. Therefore, it is necessary that He—may He be exalted—be described with those perfections.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage is a rational proof for three divine attributes: hearing (sam‘), sight (basar), and speech (kalam). Sanusi first notes that the intellect can be used to demonstrate these attributes, though transmitted evidence (al-sam‘) is even stronger. The proof proceeds as follows: Every living being capable of having a given attribute must either have it, its equivalent, or its opposite. The living being (al-hayy) is what accepts being described with these three attributes, as the dead cannot. Therefore, the basis for accepting these attributes is either life itself or something inseparable from life. Consequently, every living being must be described with these attributes. If a living being lacked them, it would have to have their opposites (deafness, blindness, muteness). These opposites are defects, and God is necessarily free from all defects by consensus of rational people. Hence, God must possess hearing, sight, and speech as perfections.

Key Terms
سمع
بصر
كلام
عقل
حي
ضد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These attributes can only be known through revelation.
Correction: Sanusi shows that reason alone can demonstrate the necessity of hearing, sight, and speech for God, because their opposites are defects.

Checkpoint
What is the key premise in the rational proof for God's attributes of hearing, sight, and speech?
A) All living beings have these attributes.
B) Every living being must have an attribute or its opposite.
C) God is described in revelation as hearing.
D) The dead cannot have attributes.

Key Takeaway
God must possess hearing, sight, and speech because their opposites are defects, and God is necessarily free from all defects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just read that God must have hearing, sight, and speech because their opposites are defects. Reflect on moments when you acted as if God did not see or hear you—perhaps in secret sin or neglect of His commands. How does this proof call you to live with constant awareness that He perceives everything? What will you change today?
?
If you truly believe God speaks (kalam), how does that transform your approach to the Qur'an? Do you listen to it as the very speech of the All-Hearing, All-Seeing? Commit to a specific way you will honor the Qur'an this week as His living word.
?
This proof relies on the consensus of rational people that God is free from defects. Have you ever doubted God's attributes due to intellectual pride or reliance on your own reasoning? How can you humbly submit to this rational proof and let it strengthen your conviction in His perfections?

Scriptural Proof for the Three Attributes and Its Superiority
Sanusi presents scriptural evidence for the three attributes and explains why it is preferred.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the scriptural proof for Allah's attributes of hearing, sight, and speech is considered superior to the rational proof, and why reason alone cannot transfer judgments from the created world to the Creator.

Core Idea
What is a perfection for creatures may not be for the Creator; revelation confirms the attributes.

Sanusi has given a rational proof for the three attributes, but now he argues that the scriptural proof is actually stronger. He explains that while these attributes appear perfect in our world, we cannot automatically transfer that judgment to Allah. This lesson explores his reasoning and the critical distinction between the witnessed (shahid) and the unseen (gha'ib).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the translation. Notice that the passage has two clear parts: the presentation of the scriptural proof and the explanation of its superiority.
Pay attention to the key terms: al-samʿ, al-shāhid, al-ghāʾib.
2
Identify the two parts of the passage
The first part states that the Book, Sunna, and consensus affirm the three attributes. The second part explains why this scriptural proof is better than the rational proof. Find where the shift occurs.
The shift is at 'Wa innamā kāna dalīlu al-samʿ...'
3
Understand the shahid-gha'ib analogy
Sanusi gives the example of pleasure and pain: they are perfections for living beings in this world, but they are impossible for Allah. This shows that not every perfection in the created world is a perfection for the Creator.
This is the core argument against relying solely on reason.
4
Grasp the role of reason and scripture
Sanusi explains that reason can only know attributes from actions (like power from creation). When reason gives no clear indication, we must turn to scripture. If scripture is silent, we stop (waqf). Since scripture explicitly affirms these attributes, we must accept them.
This establishes the methodology for Islamic theology.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this matters: it safeguards Allah's transcendence by not assuming that our human categories apply directly to Him, and it affirms the necessity of revelation for knowing Allah's attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما وجه إثباتها بالسمع ؛ أي : النقل عن الشرع : فقد صرَّحَ بإثباتها الكتاب والسنَّةُ ، وأجمعَ على ثبوتِها مَنْ يُعتد بإجماعِه كمالاً وإنَّما كانَ دليلُ السمع في هذه المسألة أُولى : لأَنَّهُ إنَّما ثبت لتلك الأوصاف الكمال في الشاهد ، ولا يلزمُ مِنْ كون الشيء في الشاهدِ أنْ يكونَ في الغائبِ كذلكَ ، ألا ترى أنَّ الالتذاذ والتألم كمالانِ للحي في الشاهد ، وهما ممتنعان على الله تعالى ؟! وذاتُهُ عزَّ وجلَّ لم تُعرَف حتى يُحكَمَ بِمُجرَّدِ العقل أنَّ هذه الصفاتِ الثلاث كمالات حقه ليصح اتصافُهُ بها ؛ بحيثُ يلزمُ إذا لم يتصف بها أَنْ يَتَّصفَ بأضدادها ، وإِنَّما نعرفُ مِنْ صفاتِهِ جلَّ وعلا بالعقل ما دلت عليهِ أفعاله ، بحيث لو لم تكن تلك الصفةُ لم يمكن أنْ يكونَ فعل مِنَ الأفعال ، فإنْ لم نجد في العقلِ دلالةً لجأنا إلى السمع ، فإن لم يرد وجب الوقفُ ، وقد وردَ السمعُ بثبوتِ هذهِ الصفاتِ الثلاثِ ، فوجبَ القطع بثبوتها
As for the way of affirming them by scripture (al-samʿ), i.e., transmission from the divine law: the Book and the Sunna have explicitly affirmed them, and those whose consensus is considered have agreed upon their establishment perfectly. And the scriptural proof in this issue is superior only because those attributes are established as perfections in the witness (al-shāhid), and it does not follow from something being in the witness that it is likewise in the absent (al-ghāʾib). Do you not see that pleasure (al-iltidhādh) and pain (al-taʾallum) are perfections for the living in the witness, yet they are impossible for Allah? And His Essence, exalted and majestic, is not known such that by mere reason one could judge that these three attributes are perfections truly due to Him so that it would be necessary for Him to be described with them, and if He is not described with them, then He would be described with their opposites. Rather, we know from His attributes, exalted and high, by reason only that which His actions indicate, such that if that attribute did not exist, no action of those actions could exist. Then if we do not find an indication in reason, we resort to scripture; if it does not come, then stopping (al-waqf) is necessary. And scripture has come affirming these three attributes, so it is necessary to be certain of their establishment.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof for the three attributes: scriptural evidence (al-samʿ) from the Qurʾan, Sunna, and consensus. The text then argues that this proof is actually superior (awlā) to the rational proof. The reason is that while these attributes appear to be perfections in our observed world (al-shāhid), we cannot automatically transfer that judgment to Allah (al-ghāʾib) because what is a perfection for creatures may not be for the Creator. The analogy of pleasure and pain is given: they are perfections for living beings here but impossible for Allah. Therefore, reason alone cannot definitively determine that hearing, sight, and speech are perfections for Allah in a way that would force the conclusion that He must have them to avoid their opposites. Reason can only tell us attributes that are necessary based on actions (e.g., power is needed to create). When reason does not give a decisive indication, we turn to scripture. Since scripture clearly affirms these three attributes, we must accept them with certainty.

السنة
الإجماع

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Reason alone can determine that hearing, sight, and speech are perfections for Allah.
Correction: The passage shows that what is a perfection in the created world may not be a perfection for Allah. Reason cannot transfer judgments from shahid to gha'ib without scriptural confirmation.

Checkpoint
Why is the scriptural proof for the three attributes considered superior to the rational proof?
A) Because the rational proof is weak.
B) Because what is a perfection in the witness may not be in the absent, so we need revelation to confirm it.
C) Because the scriptural proof is easier to understand.
D) Because the rational proof only works for one attribute.

Key Takeaway
Scripture is necessary to confirm that attributes like hearing, sight, and speech are truly perfections for Allah, because reason alone cannot transfer judgments from the created world to the Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Think of one quality you admire in yourself or others—like patience, generosity, or mercy. Have you ever assumed that God must possess that quality in exactly the same way you do? How will you train yourself to let scripture define God's attributes instead of your own experience? ?

Is there a belief about God that you hold mainly because it feels right or makes sense to you, rather than because revelation has explicitly affirmed it? Write down that belief and ask yourself: Would I still hold it if scripture were silent? If not, what will you do to align your heart with what Allah has actually revealed?
?

Correct Position on Divine Perception of Smells, Tastes, and Touches
Sanusi states that the correct position on divine perception of non-sensory objects is to stop.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the correct position regarding Allah's perception of smells, tastes, and touches is to stop (waqf), neither affirming nor denying, and the rational argument against denying it.

Core Idea
When scripture is silent, we stop — not affirm, not deny.

In the study of divine attributes, some questions are not explicitly addressed in revelation. One such issue is whether Allah perceives smells, tastes, and touches. In this passage, Sanusi clarifies that the chosen position is suspension of judgment (waqf), while also refuting those who would deny it outright.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without overthinking. Then read the literal translation to grasp the meaning.
Notice the compressed style of Sanusi's text.
2
Identify the key terms and ruling
Find the terms 'al-idrāk', 'al-waqf', and the three types of perception. Understand that 'al-waqf' means stopping, not affirming or denying.
The ruling applies specifically to smells, tastes, and touches.
3
Understand the rational argument
Read the refutation part. Why does denying Allah's perception of realities lead to absurdity? Because it gives creatures superiority over the Creator.
The argument is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Reflect on the methodology
Think about why stopping is chosen: scripture does not explicitly affirm or deny these perceptions, and reason alone cannot decide. This shows a careful, evidence-based approach.
This is a lesson in theological methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ومِنْ ثَمَّ كانَ المختارُ في الإدراك الوقف) يعني بالإدراك : إدراك المشموماتِ وإدراك المذوقاتِ وإدراك الملموساتِ ، وإنَّما لم يحتج في أصل العقيدة إلى بيان معنى هذا الإدراك ؛ لأنَّه غلبَ ( وإن أنكر منكر كونه مدركاً لحقيقة الأشياء .. فقد أثبت للمخلوق في الإحاطة والدَّرَكِ مزيَّةً على الخالق ، ولا خفاء ببطلان ذلك ، وكيف يصح في العقل أن يخلق الرب للعبد الدَّرَكَ الحقيقي وهو لا يدرك حقيقة ما خلق للعبد إدراكه ؟ ! )
His saying: (And hence the chosen position concerning perception (al-idrāk) is stopping (al-waqf).) By perception he means perception of things smelled (al-mashmūmāt), perception of things tasted (al-madhūqāt), and perception of things touched (al-malmūsāt). And indeed there was no need in the foundation of creed to explain the meaning of this perception, because it is predominant. (And if a denier denies that He is a perceiver of the reality of things, then he has affirmed for the creature, in encompassing and perceiving, a superiority over the Creator—and the falsehood of that is not hidden. And how can it be sound in reason that the Lord creates for the servant real perception while He does not perceive the reality of what He created for the servant to perceive?)
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage is a statement on a sub-issue within divine attributes: whether Allah has perception (idrāk) of non-sensory objects like smells, tastes, and touches. The commentator clarifies that the chosen position (al-mukhtār) is suspension of judgment (al-waqf)—neither affirming nor denying. The reason is that scripture does not clearly address these types of perception for Allah, and reason does not compel an answer. In the creed itself, it was unnecessary to define this perception because it is generally understood. Then the text includes a refutation of someone who denies that Allah perceives the reality of things: such a denial would imply that creatures have an advantage over the Creator in perception, which is absurd. So while we stop from making a positive or negative claim about these specific types of perception, we also reject any denial that would imply imperfection in Allah.

الشم
الذوق
اللمس
الوقف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Muslims must affirm every type of perception for Allah.
Correction: This passage shows that for some types (smells, tastes, touches), suspension is the correct approach unless scripture dictates otherwise. Affirming or denying without evidence is not required.

Checkpoint
What is the chosen position regarding Allah's perception of smells, tastes, and touches?
A) Affirmation that He perceives them.
B) Denial that He perceives them.
C) Stopping (waqf) without affirming or denying.
D) Only rational inference is used.

Key Takeaway
The correct position regarding Allah's perception of smells, tastes, and touches is to stop, neither affirming nor denying, while rejecting any denial that would imply imperfection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Debate on Divine Perception and the Preferred View of Suspension
Sanusi presents the debate on divine perception and opts for suspension.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three scholarly positions on whether God has perceptions of smell, taste, and touch, and why the suspension view is the chosen one based on methodological reliance on revelation.

Core Idea
When revelation is silent, suspend judgment on divine attributes.

Sanusi confronts a subtle theological question: does God perceive smells, tastes, and touches as additional attributes beyond His knowledge? He outlines the rational arguments and scholarly disagreements, then presents the suspension view as the most cautious and methodologically sound position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Notice the refutation of those who deny God's perception and the presentation of three opinions.
Pay attention to the embedded refutation in parentheses.
2
Identify the three perceptions
Locate where Sanusi defines 'perception' as specifically the perception of smells, tastes, and touches. Understand that these are distinct from hearing and sight.
3
Understand the refutation
Grasp the rational argument: denying God's perception of the reality of things would grant creatures superiority over the Creator in encompassing knowledge.
This refutation establishes that God must have perception in some sense.
4
Compare the three positions
Identify the three scholarly views: (1) affirmation as additional attributes (Imam al-Haramayn), (2) denial of addition (knowledge suffices), (3) suspension (the chosen view).
Note the methodological reason for suspension: lack of revelatory evidence.
5
Grasp the proof for suspension
Understand the methodological principle: for perfections known in the witnessed world, we rely on revelation. Since revelation affirms hearing, sight, and speech but not these perceptions, we suspend judgment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ومِنْ ثَمَّ كانَ المختارُ في الإدراك الوقف ( يعني بالإدراك : إدراك المشموماتِ وإدراك المذوقاتِ وإدراك الملموساتِ ، وإنَّما لم يحتج في أصل العقيدة إلى بيان معنى هذا الإدراك ؛ لأنَّه غلبَ ( وإن أنكر منكر كونه مدركاً لحقيقة الأشياء .. فقد أثبت للمخلوق في الإحاطة والدَّرَكِ مزيَّةً على الخالق ، ولا خفاء ببطلان ذلك ، وكيف يصح في العقل أن يخلق الرب للعبد الدَّرَكَ الحقيقي وهو لا يدرك حقيقة ما خلق للعبد إدراكه ؟ ! ) . الاصطلاح فيهِ عندَ الإطلاقِ على أنَّ المراد به تلك الإدراكات الثلاثةُ ، فهذه الإدراكاتُ الثلاثةُ للأشياء الثلاثةِ تقرر في الشاهدِ أَنَّها كمالات زائدة على العلم كما تقرَّرَ ذلك في السمع والبصرِ ؛ فمِنْ أجل ذلكَ جزم بثبوتِ هذه الإدراكاتِ اللهِ تعالى زائدةً على العلمِ مِنْ غيرِ جارحةٍ ولا اتصال ولا حدوثِ أمر بها للذاتِ العليَّةِ . . مَنِ اعتمد في ثبوتِ السمع والبصر على الدليل العقلي ، إذ الطريقُ في الجميع واحد ؛ وهو لزوم الاتصاف بالآفاتِ(۱) على تقدير نفي تلك الكمالاتِ ، وهذا القول هو مذهب إمام الحرمين (۲) ، ومِنَ الأَئِمَّةِ مَنْ جَزْمَ بنفْيِ زيادةِ هذه الإدراكات على علمهِ تعالى ، وجعله مغنياً عنها والتحقيق والمختارُ على ما أشار إليهِ المُقتَرَحُ وابنُ التَّلمساني رحمهما الله تعالى : الوقْفُ في هذه الإدراكات (۳) ؛ بمعنى : لا ندري أهي ثابتة له تعالى زائدةٌ على علمه ، أم هي داخلة في علمه جل وعزَّ . وحُجَّةُ هذا المختارِ : ما أومأنا إليهِ في أصل العقيدةِ مِنْ أَنَّ الأولى في إثباتِ ما تقرَّرَ أَنَّهُ كمال في الشاهدِ كالسمع والبصر والكلام.. الاعتماد على دليل الشرع ، وقد ورد في تلك الثلاثةِ ، فوجبَ إثباتها ولم يرد في هذه الإدراكاتِ الأُخرِ ، فوجبَ الوقْفُ في إثباتِها ونفيها والله سبحانَهُ أعلم .
His statement: (And from that, the chosen view regarding perception (al-idrāk) is suspension (al-waqf) — meaning by perception: perception of things smelled, perception of things tasted, and perception of things touched. And he did not need in the foundation of creed to explain the meaning of this perception because it was predominant. (And if someone denies that He is a perceiver of the reality of things... then he has affirmed for the creature an excellence in encompassing and perceiving over the Creator, and there is no concealment of the falsity of that. And how can it be sound in reason that the Lord creates for the servant true perception while He does not perceive the reality of what He created for the servant's perception?!). The technical usage in absolute terms is that what is meant is those three perceptions. So these three perceptions of the three kinds of things are established in the witnessed world as perfections additional to knowledge, just as that was established for hearing and sight. Because of that, some affirmed the existence of these perceptions to God Most High as additional to knowledge, without a limb, contact, or occurrence of any state to the Supreme Essence. Those who relied in proving hearing and sight on rational evidence—since the path in all is one—namely the necessity of being described with defects in the event of negating those perfections. This is the position of Imam al-Haramayn. Among the scholars are those who decisively affirmed the negation of these perceptions being additional to His knowledge, and made it suffice for them. But the verified view, and the chosen view as alluded to by al-Muqtrah and Ibn al-Tilimsani, may God have mercy on them, is suspension regarding these perceptions, meaning: we do not know whether they are established for Him Most High as additional to His knowledge, or are included in His knowledge, Exalted and Glorious. And the proof of this chosen view is what we indicated in the foundation of the creed: that the primary method in establishing what is established as a perfection in the witnessed world, like hearing, sight, and speech, is reliance on the proof of revelation. And it has come regarding those three, so their affirmation is necessary, but it has not come regarding these other perceptions, so suspension in affirming or negating them is necessary. And God, glorified is He, knows best.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer presentation followed by a definitive position on the issue of divine perception. The author begins by clarifying the term 'perception' as referring specifically to the perception of smells, tastes, and touches. He notes that in the foundation of creed, the precise meaning of this perception was not needed because it was understood by convention. He then includes a refutation of those who deny that God perceives the reality of things: such denial grants creatures superiority over the Creator in encompassing perception, which is absurd. After establishing that these three perceptions are perfections additional to knowledge in the witnessed world (like hearing and sight), he presents three scholarly positions: (1) some affirm these perceptions as additional to God's knowledge, using the same rational argument as for hearing and sight (the argument of avoiding defects); this is the view of Imam al-Haramayn. (2) Others deny that these perceptions are additional to knowledge, considering knowledge sufficient. (3) The chosen view, al-Muqtrah and Ibn al-Tilimsani, is suspension: we do not know whether God has these perceptions as additional attributes or whether they are encompassed by His knowledge. The proof for this suspension is the methodological principle that for perfections established in the witnessed world, we rely on revelation. Revelation has affirmed hearing, sight, and speech, so we affirm them; but revelation has not specifically affirmed these other perceptions, so we must suspend judgment, neither affirming nor denying them as additional attributes.

Key Terms
الإدراك
الوقف
الكمال
الشاهد
السمع
البصر
الكلام
علم الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that denying divine perception of specific senses makes God imperfect, implying that affirmation is necessary.
Correction: The passage shows that suspension is a valid methodological position due to lack of revelatory evidence; it does not imply imperfection, but rather caution where revelation is silent.

Checkpoint
What is the definitive position (المختار) regarding God's perception of smells, tastes, and touches?
A) Affirm them as additional attributes beyond knowledge.
B) Deny them entirely.
C) Suspend judgment, neither affirming nor denying.
D) Affirm them as identical to knowledge.

Key Takeaway
The suspension view on divine perception teaches us that for attributes not explicitly affirmed in revelation, we must refrain from both affirmation and negation, relying on methodological caution.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a matter about Allah that is not explicitly addressed in the Qur'an or Sunnah, do you have the humility to suspend judgment, or do you feel compelled to take a position? How might this lesson change your approach?
?
The scholars suspended judgment on these perceptions because revelation was silent. In your own life, are there matters of faith where you rely on your own reasoning rather than submitting to the limits of revealed knowledge? What could you learn from the principle of waqf?
?
Consider the statement: 'We do not know whether these perceptions are additional to His knowledge or encompassed by it.' Does this fill you with a sense of awe at Allah's transcendence, or does it create discomfort? How can you cultivate contentment with not knowing?

The Three Perceptions and the Waqf Position
Sanusi discusses the three perceptions and defends the suspension position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three perceptions (idrakat), the two main scholarly positions on their relation to God's knowledge, and the reasoning behind the preferred position of suspension (waqf).

Core Idea
The correct method for divine attributes relies on revelation, not rational analogy alone.

Sanusi addresses a subtle question: Are the three perceptions (idrakat) additional attributes of God beyond His knowledge? He first clarifies the term, then presents two opposing views from prominent scholars, and finally advocates for suspending judgment, grounding his position in a methodological principle about relying on transmitted evidence.

Guided Path
1
Understand the term 'idrakat'
Read the opening to grasp how Sanusi defines the three perceptions and what they refer to in the context of divine attributes.
Note that 'idrakat' here is a technical term, not generic perception.
2
Learn the two opposing positions
Identify the position of Imam al-Haramayn (rational affirmation) and the position of those who negate addition, understanding their rationales.
Both positions rely on different methodological assumptions.
3
Discover the chosen position of waqf
Focus on the definition of waqf and its proof: that revelation has come for hearing, sight, and speech, but not for these perceptions, so we suspend judgment.
This is the key methodological lesson.
4
Reflect on the principle of reliance on revelation
Consider why Sanusi prioritizes transmitted evidence over pure rational analogy in matters of divine attributes.
This principle is central to Ash'ari methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاصطلاح فيهِ عندَ الإطلاقِ على أنَّ المراد به تلك الإدراكات الثلاثةُ ، فهذه الإدراكاتُ الثلاثةُ للأشياء الثلاثةِ تقرر في الشاهدِ أَنَّها كمالات زائدة على العلم كما تقرَّرَ ذلك في السمع والبصرِ ؛ فمِنْ أجل ذلكَ جزم بثبوتِ هذه الإدراكاتِ اللهِ تعالى زائدةً على العلمِ مِنْ غيرِ جارحةٍ ولا اتصال ولا حدوثِ أمر بها للذاتِ العليَّةِ . . مَنِ اعتمد في ثبوتِ السمع والبصر على الدليل العقلي ، إذ الطريقُ في الجميع واحد ؛ وهو لزوم الاتصاف بالآفاتِ على تقدير نفي تلك الكمالاتِ ، وهذا القول هو مذهب إمام الحرمين ، ومِنَ الأَئِمَّةِ مَنْ جَزْمَ بنفْيِ زيادةِ هذه الإدراكات على علمهِ تعالى ، وجعله مغنياً عنها. والتحقيق والمختارُ على ما أشار إليهِ المُقتَرَحُ وابنُ التَّلمساني رحمهما الله تعالى : الوقْفُ في هذه الإدراكات ؛ بمعنى : لا ندري أهي ثابتة له تعالى زائدةٌ على علمه ، أم هي داخلة في علمه جل وعزَّ . وحُجَّةُ هذا المختارِ : ما أومأنا إليهِ في أصل العقيدةِ مِنْ أَنَّ الأولى في إثباتِ ما تقرَّرَ أَنَّهُ كمال في الشاهدِ كالسمع والبصر والكلام.. الاعتماد على دليل الشرع ، وقد ورد في تلك الثلاثةِ ، فوجبَ إثباتها ولم يرد في هذه الإدراكاتِ الأُخرِ ، فوجبَ الوقْفُ في إثباتِها ونفيها. والله سبحانَهُ أعلم .
The terminology, when used absolutely, is that what is meant by it is those three perceptions. So these three perceptions of the three things are established in the witnessed realm as perfections additional to knowledge, just as that is established in the case of hearing and sight. For that reason, it was decisively affirmed that these perceptions exist for God, exalted, additional to knowledge, without any organ, connection, or occurrence of anything in the Divine Essence. Whoever relies in affirming hearing and sight on rational proof—since the way in all is one, namely the necessity of being described with defects if those perfections are negated—this statement is the school of the Imam of the Two Sanctuaries. And among the imams is one who decisively negates the addition of these perceptions to His knowledge, exalted, and deems that knowledge suffices for them. The verification and the chosen view, as indicated by al-Muqtrah and Ibn al-Tilimsani (may God have mercy on them), is suspension (al-waqf) regarding these perceptions: meaning, we do not know whether they are established for Him, exalted, additional to His knowledge, or are included within His knowledge, mighty and majestic. The proof of this chosen view is what we hinted at in the original creed: that the primary [principle] in affirming what is established as a perfection in the witnessed realm, like hearing, sight, and speech, is reliance on transmitted evidence. And [transmitted evidence] has come concerning those three, so their affirmation became obligatory, and it has not come concerning these other perceptions, so suspension became obligatory regarding their affirmation and negation. And God, glorified, knows best.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is a theological discussion on the nature of three perceptions (idrakat) relative to God's knowledge. The author begins by clarifying a term: when the term is used absolutely, it refers to these three perceptions. These perceptions are understood in the empirical world as perfections additional to knowledge, similar to hearing and sight being additional perfections. Consequently, one might think they should be affirmed for God as additional to His knowledge, but without any physical organ, connection, or temporal occurrence. The author then presents two opposing positions. The first is that of Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni), who relies on rational proof: if these perfections were negated, God would be described with defects, so they must be affirmed. The second position is held by some imams who deny that these perceptions are additional to God's knowledge, considering knowledge sufficient. The author then states that the verified and chosen position, following al-Muqtrah and Ibn al-Tilimsani, is waqf (suspension). This means we do not know whether these perceptions are additional to God's knowledge or included within it. The proof for this suspension is methodological: in matters where a perfection is established in the empirical realm (like hearing, sight, and speech), the primary reliance should be on transmitted evidence (divine revelation). For the three well-known attributes (hearing, sight, speech), revelation has come, so they are affirmed. But for these other perceptions, no revelation has come, so we must suspend judgment. The passage concludes with 'And God knows best.'

Key Terms
الإدراكات (al-idrakat)
الوقف (al-waqf)
الكمال (al-kamal)
السمع (al-sam‘)
البصر (al-basar)
الكلام (al-kalam)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that since hearing and sight are additional perfections in humans, they must be additional to God's knowledge by rational necessity.
Correction: Sanusi shows that the correct method is to rely on revelation for such attributes, and since revelation does not affirm addition for other perceptions, we suspend judgment.

Checkpoint
What is the chosen position regarding the three perceptions (idrakat) and why?
A) They are affirmed as additional to knowledge based on rational proof.
B) They are negated as additional to knowledge because knowledge suffices.
C) Suspension (waqf) is chosen because no transmitted evidence affirms them.
D) They are affirmed as included within knowledge based on consensus.

Key Takeaway
The correct approach to divine attributes is to rely on revelation when available, and suspend judgment when not, as exemplified by the waqf position on the three perceptions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there areas of your faith where you have been quick to affirm or deny something about God without clear revelation? How can you adopt the waqf attitude of humility and reliance on scripture starting today?
?
When you encounter a theological question that scripture does not explicitly address, do you feel the pressure to have an answer? Can you rest in not knowing, trusting that God knows best, and commit to suspending judgment rather than speculating?
?
Will you commit to seeking scriptural evidence before forming a firm belief about any divine attribute, and if revelation is silent, will you humbly say 'I do not know' instead of relying on your own reasoning?

Three Opinions on Sam‘iyyat Attributes and the Eight Essential Attributes
Sanusi presents three opinions on istiwa', yad, 'ayn, wajh and defines the eight essential attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three scholarly positions on the four sam‘iyyat attributes (istiwa’, yad, ‘ayn, wajh) and the definition and classification of the eight essential attributes.

Core Idea
The four ambiguous attributes are interpreted in three ways, while the eight essential attributes are clearly defined.

This passage by Sanusi addresses a key question in Islamic theology: how do we understand terms like 'hand' and 'eye' when attributed to Allah? He presents three classic opinions—those of al-Ash‘ari, al-Juwayni, and the Salaf. Then he clarifies what he means by the 'eight attributes,' listing them and explaining which are known by reason and which by revelation. This dual focus helps the student see the broader framework of divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the two main sections: the three opinions on the four terms, and the list of the eight attributes.
2
Identify the three opinions
The passage names three opinions: (1) the attributes are real beyond the eight, (2) they are interpreted metaphorically, (3) they are consigned to God with tanzih. Understand each.
All opinions agree on tanzih.
3
Understand the eight attributes
The passage defines the eight existential attributes. Note that seven are certain, and the eighth (idrak) has disagreement. Also note the classification by reason and text.
4
Connect the sections
See that the four terms are discussed because they are additional attributes that might be considered sam‘iyyat. The eight attributes are the baseline.
5
Reflect on the principle
All opinions agree on tanzih. The disagreement is only on how to handle the apparent meaning.

الكلام على الصفاتِ السمعيَّةِ غيرِ الثمانيةِ على القول : وفي كون الاستواء واليد والعين والوجه أسماءً لصفات غير الثمانية ، أو مُؤوّلةً بالاستيلاء والقدرة والبصر والوجودِ ، أو يُوقَفُ عن تأويلها وتُفوَّضُ معانيها إلى اللهِ تعالى ، بعد التنزيه عن ظواهرها المستحيلة إجماعاً . . ثلاثة أقوال ؛ للشيخ الأشعري ، وإمام الحرمين ، والسلف يعني بالصفاتِ الثمانية : الصفاتِ الوجودية؛ صفات وهي المعاني؛ فمنها سبعة مقطوع بثبوتها له جلَّ وعزَّ؛ وهي العلم والقدرة والإرادة والحياةُ والسمع والبصر والكلام، أربعة منها بالعقل لتوقفِ الفعل عليها؛ وهي ما قبل السمع، وثلاثة بالنص، وفي ثبوتها بالعقل خلافُ؛ وهي السمع وما بعده، وأما الصفةُ الثامنة فهي الإدراك وقد تقدَّمَ فيه ثلاثة أقوال، والمختارُ : الوقف . وأشرتُ هنا إلى أنَّهُ اختُلِفَ في أشياءَ وردَتْ في الشرع مضافةً إلى الله تعالى؛ وهي الاستواء واليد والعين والوجه، بعد القطع بتنزهه تعالى عن ظواهرها المستحيلة عقلاً وإجماعاً :
Discussion on the attributes derived from revelation (al-sifat al-sam‘iyya) other than the eight, according to the position: and concerning whether al-istiwa’, al-yad, al-‘ayn, and al-wajh are names for attributes other than the eight, or are interpreted (mu’awwala) as al-istila’, al-qudra, al-basar, and al-wujud, or whether one refrains from interpreting them and consigns their meanings to God, exalted, after declaring Him free from their impossible apparent meanings by consensus—there are three opinions: of al-Shaykh al-Ash‘ari, Imam al-Haramayn, and the Salaf. He means by the eight attributes: the existential attributes (al-sifat al-wujudiyya), attributes which are meanings (ma‘ani). Among them are seven whose establishment for Him, mighty and majestic, is decisively affirmed: knowledge, power, will, life, hearing, sight, and speech. Four of them are [affirmed] by reason because action depends on them, and these are those before hearing; three are [affirmed] by textual proof (al-nass), and there is disagreement on their establishment by reason—these are hearing and what follows it. As for the eighth attribute, it is perception (al-idrak), concerning which three opinions have preceded, and the chosen one is suspension (al-waqf). And I have indicated here that there is disagreement concerning things that have come in revelation as attributed to God, exalted: namely al-istiwa’, al-yad, al-‘ayn, and al-wajh, after definitively declaring Him free from their impossible apparent meanings, by reason and by consensus:
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is a classification and discussion of the attributes of God. It begins by addressing the 'sam‘iyyat' attributes—those known primarily from revelation—other than the eight essential attributes. The author states that there are three opinions regarding four specific terms: istiwa’ (often translated as 'establishing Himself'), yad (hand), ‘ayn (eye), and wajh (face). The first opinion, attributed to al-Ash‘ari, holds that these are names for real attributes beyond the eight. The second opinion, attributed to Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni), interprets them metaphorically: istiwa’ as istila’ (dominion), yad as qudra (power), ‘ayn as basar (sight), and wajh as wujud (existence). The third opinion, attributed to the Salaf, is to refrain from interpretation (tawqif) and consign the true meanings to God, after explicitly affirming God's transcendence beyond the literal meanings that are impossible for Him, a point agreed upon by consensus. The passage then defines what is meant by 'the eight attributes'. They are the existential attributes (al-sifat al-wujudiyya), which are meanings (ma‘ani) inhering in the essence. Seven of these are definitively established for God: knowledge, power, will, life, hearing, sight, and speech. The author further classifies these seven: four (knowledge, power, will, life) are known by reason because rational reflection shows that action depends on them; these precede hearing in the list. The remaining three (hearing, sight, speech) are known by textual proof (nass), and there is scholarly disagreement as to whether they can also be established by reason alone. The eighth attribute is perception (idrak), about which three opinions have already been discussed earlier (referencing the previous lesson), with the chosen opinion being suspension (waqf). Finally, the author notes that he has indicated here that there is disagreement over those four terms (istiwa’, yad, ‘ayn, wajh) that appear in revelation, after the definitive consensus that God is transcendent beyond their literal, impossible meanings.

الصفات السمعية (al-sifat al-sam‘iyya)
الاستواء (al-istiwa')
اليد (al-yad)
العين (al-‘ayn)
الوجه (al-wajh)
التأويل (al-ta’wil)
التفويض (al-tafwid)
الصفات الوجودية (al-sifat al-wujudiyya)
الإدراك (al-idrak)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Salaf interpreted these verses literally without tanzih.
Correction: All three opinions, including the Salaf, affirm tanzih (transcendence) beyond the impossible literal meanings; the Salaf refrain from interpretation but do not affirm literal anthropomorphism.

Checkpoint

A) They are real attributes beyond the eight.
B) They are interpreted as istila’, qudra, basar, and wujud.
C) Their meanings are consigned to God without interpretation.
D) They are denied altogether.

Key Takeaway
The four ambiguous sam‘iyyat attributes are subject to three opinions, all affirming tanzih, while the eight essential attributes are clearly defined with seven certain and one disputed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that all three opinions agree on tanzih—Allah is beyond any human-like attributes. When you read verses describing Allah's 'hand' or 'face,' do you find your heart slipping into imagining a physical form? What concrete step will you take to train your mind to transcend such images and affirm His incomparability?
?
The passage lists seven attributes that are decisively affirmed for Allah. Which of these seven do you feel most deeply in your daily worship—knowledge, power, will, life, hearing, sight, or speech? Which one is most absent from your awareness right now, and what will you do to bring that attribute into your consciousness before you sleep tonight?
?
The eighth attribute, perception (idrak), is left suspended by the chosen opinion. Does your soul feel a tension in not knowing exactly what it means? Can you trust Allah's perfection even when your intellect cannot fully grasp it, and how will you surrender that discomfort to Him in prayer this evening?

The Eight Existential Attributes
Sanusi defines the eight existential attributes and their bases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what the eight existential attributes are, which seven are definitively established, and the status of the eighth (perception).

Core Idea
Seven of the eight attributes are certain; the eighth is debated.

Before discussing non-eight revealed attributes, Sanusi clarifies the eight existential attributes. These are the attributes of meaning subsisting in God's essence. Seven are definitively established by reason or revelation, while the eighth, perception, has three opinions. This lesson lays the foundation for understanding why additional attributes are controversial.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the eight attributes
Read the Arabic passage that defines the eight existential attributes and identifies the seven definitively established ones.
Notice that the author uses 'ya'ni' to explain.
2
Identify the seven definitive attributes
List the seven attributes: knowledge, power, will, life, hearing, sight, speech. Note which are established by reason (first four) and which by text (last three).
Reason establishes attributes necessary for action.
3
Understand the eighth attribute
The eighth attribute is perception (al-idrak). Read the three opinions on it and the chosen view of waqf (stopping).
Waqf means neither affirming nor denying a specific meaning.
4
Connect to the next lesson
Realize that the non-eight revealed attributes are additional to these eight, and the controversy arises because they are only known through revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام على الصفاتِ السمعيَّةِ غيرِ الثمانيةِ على القول : وفي كون الاستواء واليد والعين والوجه أسماءً لصفات غير الثمانية ، أو مُؤوّلةً بالاستيلاء والقدرة والبصر والوجودِ ، أو يُوقَفُ عن تأويلها وتُفوَّضُ معانيها إلى اللهِ تعالى ، بعد التنزيه عن ظواهرها المستحيلة إجماعاً . . ثلاثة أقوال ؛ للشيخ الأشعري ، وإمام الحرمين ، والسلف . يعني بالصفاتِ الثمانية : الصفاتِ الوجودية وهي المعاني ؛ فمنها سبعة مقطوع بثبوتها له جلَّ وعزَّ ؛ وهي العلم والقدرة والإرادة والحياةُ والسمع والبصر والكلام ، أربعة منها بالعقل لتوقفِ الفعل عليها ؛ وهي ما قبل السمع ، وثلاثة بالنص ، وفي ثبوتها بالعقل خلافُ ؛ وهي السمع وما بعده ، وأما الصفةُ الثامنة فهي الإدراك وقد تقدَّمَ فيه ثلاثة أقوال ، والمختارُ : الوقف . وأشرتُ هنا إلى أنَّهُ اختُلِفَ في أشياءَ وردَتْ في الشرع مضافةً إلى الله تعالى ؛ وهي الاستواء واليد والعين والوجه ، بعد القطع بتنزهه تعالى عن ظواهرها المستحيلة عقلاً وإجماعاً : فقال الشيخ أبو الحسن الأشعري : إنَّها أسماء لصفات تقوم بذاتِهِ زائدة على الصفاتِ الثمانية السابقة ، والسبيلُ عندَهُ إلى إثباتها السمعُ لا العقل ، ولهذا تُسمَّى على مذهبه صفاتٍ سمعيَّةً ، والله تعالى أعلم بحقيقتها . ومذهب إمام الحرمين : تأويلها بما ذكرناه في أصل العقيدة . ومذهب السلف : الوقْفُ في تأويل تعيينها ، وقالوا : نقطعُ بأنَّ ظاهرها المستحيل غيرُ مرادٍ ، ونفوِّضُ بعد ذلك عين المراد منها إلى الله تعالى ؛ لصحة حمل اللفظ على محامل ، ولم يعيّن الشارع المراد منها ، فتعيين بعضها بغير نقل عن صاحب الشرع تجاسر على الغيب بغير دليل ، وهذا القولُ هو أحسنُ الأقوال وأسلمها .
Discussion on the revealed attributes other than the eight, according to the view: Regarding whether al-istiwa', al-yad, al-'ayn, and al-wajh are names for attributes other than the eight, or interpreted metaphorically as al-istila', al-qudra, al-basr, and al-wujud, or one stops from interpreting them and delegates their meanings to Allah Almighty, after declaring His transcendence above their impossible apparent meanings by consensus — three opinions: of al-Shaykh al-Ash'ari, Imam al-Haramayn, and the Salaf. He means by the eight attributes: the existential attributes, which are the meanings; among them seven are definitively established for Him, Glorified and Exalted: knowledge, power, will, life, hearing, sight, and speech. Four of them are by reason due to the dependence of action upon them — those before hearing — and three by text, and there is disagreement regarding their establishment by reason — they are hearing and what follows it. As for the eighth attribute, it is perception (al-idrak), and there have been three opinions about it, and the chosen is stopping (al-waqf). And I have indicated here that there is disagreement regarding things that have come in the Law attributed to Allah Almighty: al-istiwa', al-yad, al-'ayn, and al-wajh, after determining His transcendence above their impossible apparent meanings by reason and consensus. So al-Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari said: They are names for attributes subsisting in His essence, additional to the previous eight attributes, and the way to establish them according to him is revelation, not reason, and for this they are called in his school 'revealed attributes', and Allah Almighty knows best their reality. The doctrine of Imam al-Haramayn is to interpret them metaphorically as we have mentioned in the original creed. The doctrine of the Salaf is to stop regarding the determination of their interpretation, and they said: We are certain that their impossible apparent meaning is not intended, and we delegate thereafter the specific intended meaning to Allah Almighty, due to the validity of carrying the word on multiple meanings, and the Lawgiver did not specify the intended meaning, so specifying some of them without transmission from the author of the Law is an audacity regarding the unseen without evidence. And this opinion is the best of opinions and the safest.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is a comparative doctrinal discussion of three Sunni positions on a class of divine attributes that are known only through revelation (al-sifat al-sam'iyya), namely al-istiwa' (establishing above the throne), al-yad (hand), al-'ayn (eye), and al-wajh (face). The author first clarifies that by 'the eight attributes' he means the existential attributes that are meanings subsisting in God's essence. Seven are definitively established: knowledge, power, will, life, hearing, sight, and speech. Four of these (knowledge, power, will, life) are known by reason because action depends on them; three (hearing, sight, speech) are known by text, with disagreement over their rational proof. The eighth attribute is perception (al-idrak), on which there are three opinions, the preferred one being to stop (al-waqf). Then the author turns to the four attributes mentioned in revelation (istiwa', yad, 'ayn, wajh). After affirming that God is transcendent above the impossible literal meanings by both reason and consensus, he presents three positions. The first is that of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari: these are real attributes subsisting in God's essence, additional to the eight, but known only through revelation, not reason—hence they are called 'revealed attributes'. Their true nature is known only to Allah. The second is that of Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni): he interprets them metaphorically (ta'wil), e.g., istiwa' as istila' (dominion), yad as qudra (power), etc. The third is that of the Salaf (early Muslims): they stop short of assigning a specific interpretation (waqf) after negating the impossible literal meaning. They delegate the true meaning to Allah, because the word can bear multiple interpretations and the Lawgiver has not specified which is intended. To specify any particular meaning without evidence from the Law is an unjustified intrusion into the unseen. The author concludes that this third position is the best and safest.

الصفات الوجودية
المعاني
العلم
القدرة
الإرادة
الحياة
السمع
البصر
الكلام
الإدراك
الوقف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All eight existential attributes are equally and definitively established without any difference in their basis.
Correction: Only seven are definitively established. The eighth (perception) has three opinions, and the chosen view is to stop (waqf). Moreover, the seven differ in their basis: four by reason, three by text.

Checkpoint

A) All eight
B) Seven, with the eighth being subject to disagreement
C) Six, with two being uncertain
D) Five, with three being uncertain

Key Takeaway
Seven of the eight existential attributes are definitively established; the eighth (perception) is debated, with waqf as the preferred position.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You affirm that God has knowledge, power, will, and life by reason. When you act today, in what immediate way will you remind yourself that every action depends on these attributes? Commit to one concrete moment of mindfulness.
?
Sanusi stops short of defining perception (idrāk) for God. Is there an aspect of God’s nature that you feel uncomfortable leaving undefined? Will you trust the scholarly stance of waqf, or does your heart demand certainty? What does that urge reveal about your reliance on your own intellect over revelation?
?
You claim God hears, sees, and speaks because the text says so. When was the last time a verse about God's hearing changed what you said, or a verse about His sight changed what you did? If it has been a while, what is blocking you? Resolve to act on one such verse before tonight.

Three Positions on Non-Eight Revealed Attributes
Sanusi presents three Sunni positions on four specific revealed attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three Sunni positions on attributes like istiwa', yad, 'ayn, and wajh: the Ash'ari position of affirming real additional attributes, the Juwayni position of metaphorical interpretation, and the Salaf position of stopping and delegating.

Core Idea
Three paths: affirm real attributes, interpret metaphorically, or delegate meaning to Allah.

After clarifying the eight existential attributes, Sanusi turns to four attributes mentioned in revelation: istiwa', yad, 'ayn, and wajh. He presents three classical Sunni positions: that of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni), and the Salaf. All three agree that the literal apparent meanings are impossible for God, but they diverge on whether these are real additional attributes, metaphorical expressions, or matters to be delegated to Allah without specification.

Guided Path
1
Read the entire passage on the three positions
Read the Arabic from the summary of the three positions through the detailed explanation of each. Notice the common starting point: negation of the literal meaning.
The passage begins with 'الكلام على الصفاتِ السمعيَّةِ غيرِ الثمانية'.
2
Understand al-Ash'ari's position
Al-Ash'ari holds that these are real attributes subsisting in God's essence, additional to the eight, known only through revelation. Their true reality is known only to Allah.
They are called 'revealed attributes' (sifāt sam'iyya) in his school.
3
Understand al-Juwayni's position
Imam al-Haramayn interprets them metaphorically (ta'wil), e.g., istiwa' as istila' (dominion), yad as qudra (power), etc. This is what Sanusi referenced earlier in the creed.
This position uses reason to assign a figurative meaning.
4
Understand the Salaf's position
The Salaf stop (waqf) from assigning a specific interpretation. They negate the impossible literal meaning and delegate the true meaning to Allah. They argue that specifying without evidence is audacity.
Sanusi calls this 'the best and safest opinion'.
5
Reflect on the differences
Compare how each position handles the same revealed texts. Note that all agree on transcendence above literal meanings, but differ on what positive statement to make about the attributes.
The Ash'ari position affirms real unknown attributes; Juwayni affirms known metaphorical meanings; Salaf affirm nothing beyond negation and delegation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام على الصفاتِ السمعيَّةِ غيرِ الثمانيةِ على القول : وفي كون الاستواء واليد والعين والوجه أسماءً لصفات غير الثمانية ، أو مُؤوّلةً بالاستيلاء والقدرة والبصر والوجودِ ، أو يُوقَفُ عن تأويلها وتُفوَّضُ معانيها إلى اللهِ تعالى ، بعد التنزيه عن ظواهرها المستحيلة إجماعاً . . ثلاثة أقوال ؛ للشيخ الأشعري ، وإمام الحرمين ، والسلف . يعني بالصفاتِ الثمانية : الصفاتِ الوجودية وهي المعاني ؛ فمنها سبعة مقطوع بثبوتها له جلَّ وعزَّ ؛ وهي العلم والقدرة والإرادة والحياةُ والسمع والبصر والكلام ، أربعة منها بالعقل لتوقفِ الفعل عليها ؛ وهي ما قبل السمع ، وثلاثة بالنص ، وفي ثبوتها بالعقل خلافُ ؛ وهي السمع وما بعده ، وأما الصفةُ الثامنة فهي الإدراك وقد تقدَّمَ فيه ثلاثة أقوال ، والمختارُ : الوقف . وأشرتُ هنا إلى أنَّهُ اختُلِفَ في أشياءَ وردَتْ في الشرع مضافةً إلى الله تعالى ؛ وهي الاستواء واليد والعين والوجه ، بعد القطع بتنزهه تعالى عن ظواهرها المستحيلة عقلاً وإجماعاً : فقال الشيخ أبو الحسن الأشعري : إنَّها أسماء لصفات تقوم بذاتِهِ زائدة على الصفاتِ الثمانية السابقة ، والسبيلُ عندَهُ إلى إثباتها السمعُ لا العقل ، ولهذا تُسمَّى على مذهبه صفاتٍ سمعيَّةً ، والله تعالى أعلم بحقيقتها . ومذهب إمام الحرمين : تأويلها بما ذكرناه في أصل العقيدة . ومذهب السلف : الوقْفُ في تأويل تعيينها ، وقالوا : نقطعُ بأنَّ ظاهرها المستحيل غيرُ مرادٍ ، ونفوِّضُ بعد ذلك عين المراد منها إلى الله تعالى ؛ لصحة حمل اللفظ على محامل ، ولم يعيّن الشارع المراد منها ، فتعيين بعضها بغير نقل عن صاحب الشرع تجاسر على الغيب بغير دليل ، وهذا القولُ هو أحسنُ الأقوال وأسلمها .
Discussion on the revealed attributes other than the eight, according to the view: Regarding whether al-istiwa', al-yad, al-'ayn, and al-wajh are names for attributes other than the eight, or interpreted metaphorically as al-istila', al-qudra, al-basr, and al-wujud, or one stops from interpreting them and delegates their meanings to Allah Almighty, after declaring His transcendence above their impossible apparent meanings by consensus — three opinions: of al-Shaykh al-Ash'ari, Imam al-Haramayn, and the Salaf. He means by the eight attributes: the existential attributes, which are the meanings; among them seven are definitively established for Him, Glorified and Exalted: knowledge, power, will, life, hearing, sight, and speech. Four of them are by reason due to the dependence of action upon them — those before hearing — and three by text, and there is disagreement regarding their establishment by reason — they are hearing and what follows it. As for the eighth attribute, it is perception (al-idrak), and there have been three opinions about it, and the chosen is stopping (al-waqf). And I have indicated here that there is disagreement regarding things that have come in the Law attributed to Allah Almighty: al-istiwa', al-yad, al-'ayn, and al-wajh, after determining His transcendence above their impossible apparent meanings by reason and consensus. So al-Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari said: They are names for attributes subsisting in His essence, additional to the previous eight attributes, and the way to establish them according to him is revelation, not reason, and for this they are called in his school 'revealed attributes', and Allah Almighty knows best their reality. The doctrine of Imam al-Haramayn is to interpret them metaphorically as we have mentioned in the original creed. The doctrine of the Salaf is to stop regarding the determination of their interpretation, and they said: We are certain that their impossible apparent meaning is not intended, and we delegate thereafter the specific intended meaning to Allah Almighty, due to the validity of carrying the word on multiple meanings, and the Lawgiver did not specify the intended meaning, so specifying some of them without transmission from the author of the Law is an audacity regarding the unseen without evidence. And this opinion is the best of opinions and the safest.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is a comparative doctrinal discussion of three Sunni positions on a class of divine attributes that are known only through revelation (al-sifat al-sam'iyya), namely al-istiwa' (establishing above the throne), al-yad (hand), al-'ayn (eye), and al-wajh (face). The author first clarifies that by 'the eight attributes' he means the existential attributes that are meanings subsisting in God's essence. Seven are definitively established: knowledge, power, will, life, hearing, sight, and speech. Four of these (knowledge, power, will, life) are known by reason because action depends on them; three (hearing, sight, speech) are known by text, with disagreement over their rational proof. The eighth attribute is perception (al-idrak), on which there are three opinions, the preferred one being to stop (al-waqf). Then the author turns to the four attributes mentioned in revelation (istiwa', yad, 'ayn, wajh). After affirming that God is transcendent above the impossible literal meanings by both reason and consensus, he presents three positions. The first is that of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari: these are real attributes subsisting in God's essence, additional to the eight, but known only through revelation, not reason—hence they are called 'revealed attributes'. Their true nature is known only to Allah. The second is that of Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni): he interprets them metaphorically (ta'wil), e.g., istiwa' as istila' (dominion), yad as qudra (power), etc. The third is that of the Salaf (early Muslims): they stop short of assigning a specific interpretation (waqf) after negating the impossible literal meaning. They delegate the true meaning to Allah, because the word can bear multiple interpretations and the Lawgiver has not specified which is intended. To specify any particular meaning without evidence from the Law is an unjustified intrusion into the unseen. The author concludes that this third position is the best and safest.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Salaf's position of tafwid means they affirm a literal meaning for God's attributes without qualification.
Correction: The Salaf explicitly negate the impossible literal meaning and delegate the true meaning to Allah. They do not affirm any specific meaning; they stop at the apparent impossible meaning.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the key difference between al-Ash'ari's position and the Salaf's position on attributes like al-yad?
A) Al-Ash'ari denies them; Salaf affirm them literally.
B) Al-Ash'ari affirms them as real attributes known by reason; Salaf interpret them metaphorically.
C) Al-Ash'ari affirms them as real attributes known only by revelation; Salaf stop at negating the literal meaning and delegate the true meaning to Allah.
D) Al-Ash'ari interprets them metaphorically; Salaf take them literally.

Key Takeaway
For non-eight revealed attributes, the safest position is that of the Salaf: negate the impossible literal meaning and entrust the true meaning to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read a verse about Allah's hand or eye, do you feel unsettled by not having a precise mental image? What does that discomfort reveal about your need to control even your understanding of Allah? Are you willing to stand before Him with 'I don't know' as your answer?
?
The Salaf's position is 'safest' because it refrains from assigning meaning without evidence. Is there a revealed matter in your life—perhaps not an attribute but a ruling or decree—where you have added your own interpretation because the clear text didn't satisfy you? Will you commit to stopping at what Allah has said and entrusting the rest to Him?
?
Which of these three positions do you find yourself naturally gravitating towards? Is it because it gives you intellectual resolution, or because it deepens your awe and submission? If the former, how might you train your soul to prefer the safety of divine delegation over the comfort of human reasoning?

Three Sunni Positions on the Attributes of Hearing
Sanusi classifies three Sunni views on al-ṣifāt al-samʿiyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three major Sunni positions on how to interpret the auditory attributes (al-ṣifāt al-samʿiyya) and why the Salaf's position is considered the safest.

Core Idea
The three positions on auditory attributes reflect different methods of balancing revelation and reason.

In this passage, Sanusi presents the three approaches to the divine attributes that are known through revelation rather than reason. These are the 'auditory attributes' (al-ṣifāt al-samʿiyya). Each of the three views is attributed to a major figure or school within Ashʿarism. As you read, notice how each view handles the tension between affirming God's attributes and avoiding anthropomorphism.

Guided Path
1
Read and list the three positions
First, read the Arabic or translation and identify the three views: those of al-Ashʿari, al-Juwaynī, and the Salaf. Notice how each is described.
The passage explicitly names each view.
2
Compare the three approaches
Think about what distinguishes each view: al-Ashʿari affirms real attributes known by revelation, al-Juwaynī interprets them metaphorically, the Salaf consign the meaning to God.
The author declares the Salaf's view as 'the best and safest'.
3
Reflect on the common Sunni ground
The passage ends by noting that all three views are Sunni. Consider how this classification shows the diversity within orthodoxy.
This is important for understanding intra-Sunni debates.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقال الشيخ أبو الحسن الأشعري : إنها أسماء لصفات تقوم بذاته زائدة على الصفات الثمانية السابقة ، والسبيل عنده إلى إثباتها السمع لا العقل ، ولهذا تسمى على مذهبه صفات سمعية ، والله تعالى أعلم بحقيقتها ومذهب إمام الحرمين : تأويلها بما ذكرناه في أصل العقيدة . ومذهب السلف : الوقف في تأويل تعيينها ، وقالوا : نقطع بأن ظاهرها المستحيل غير مراد ، ونفوض بعد ذلك عين المراد منها إلى الله تعالى ؛ لصحة حمل اللفظ على محامل ، ولم يعين الشارع المراد منها ، فتعيين بعضها بغير نقل عن صاحب الشرع تجاسر على الغيب بغير دليل ، وهذا القول هو أحسن الأقوال وأسلمها . وبه تعلم: أن الأقوال المذكورة قال بها الأشاعرة ، فهي كلها أقوال سنية
The Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Ashʿari said: They are names of attributes that subsist in His essence, additional to the eight previous attributes, and the way to affirm them according to him is revelation (samʿ), not reason, and therefore in his school they are called 'auditory attributes' (ṣifāt samʿiyya), and Allah Most High knows their true reality. The school of Imam al-Ḥaramayn (al-Juwaynī) is to interpret them (taʾwīl) in the way we mentioned in the section on the creed. The school of the Salaf is to stop (al-waqf) regarding the interpretation of their specific meaning, and they said: We are certain that their impossible apparent meaning is not intended, and we consign after that the exact intended meaning to Allah Most High, due to the possibility of the word bearing multiple meanings, and the Lawgiver did not specify the intended meaning, so specifying some of them without a transmitted report from the Lawgiver is an impertinence against the unseen without proof. This opinion is the best and safest of the opinions. And by this you know that the mentioned opinions were held by the Ashʿarites, so all of them are Sunni opinions.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage presents and classifies the three major positions among Sunni theologians (Ashʿarites) on how to interpret the so-called 'auditory attributes' (al-ṣifāt al-samʿiyya) – those attributes beyond the eight essential attributes that are affirmed based on scriptural evidence rather than reason. The first position, attributed to Abu al-Hasan al-Ashʿari, is that these are real attributes subsisting in God's essence, additional to the eight, but known only through revelation, not reason, hence their name. The second position, of Imam al-Ḥaramayn (al-Juwaynī), is to interpret them metaphorically (taʾwīl) as explained in the creed. The third position, of the Salaf (early Muslims), is to stop short of any specific interpretation; they affirm that the impossible apparent meaning is not intended, but they consign the true meaning to God, since the word can have multiple meanings and the Lawgiver did not specify which one. The author then declares this third view as the best and safest. He concludes that all these opinions are Sunni opinions held by the Ashʿarites.

Misconception: The Salaf take the literal meaning of auditory attributes, implying anthropomorphism.
Correction: The Salaf are certain the literal meaning is not intended and consign the true meaning to God (tafwīḍ).

Key Takeaway
The three Sunni positions on auditory attributes show that orthodoxy includes affirmation, interpretation, and consignment, with the Salaf's view being the safest.

The Salaf's position is described as the 'best and safest' because it avoids presumptuous speculation without proof. The Shaykh's Method for Auditory Attributes
Sanusi presents the Shaykh's scriptural arguments for istiwā', yad, ʿayn, and wajh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Shaykh al-Ash'ari uses the principle of specification (takhṣīṣ) to affirm the auditory attributes from the Qur'an while rejecting both literalism and figurative interpretation.

Core Idea
The Qur'an's specification of certain attributes proves they are real, not just power or domination.

In this passage, Sanusi presents the method of Shaykh al-Ash'ari for affirming the so-called auditory attributes (ṣifāt sam'iyya). Unlike those who negate their apparent meanings or interpret them away, the Shaykh takes the verses' wording seriously, using the principle that God's specification of particular things (like the Throne, Adam's creation) indicates a real attribute. This lesson walks through his arguments for istiwā', yad, ʿayn, and wajh.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once, then the full translation. Notice how the Shaykh argues for each attribute sequentially.
The passage ends mid-sentence for wajh; the pattern is clear.
2
Identify the two rejected interpretations for istiwā'
The Shaykh rejects both the literal meaning (settling) and the figurative meaning (domination). Understand why each is rejected: the first is impossible, the second makes specification meaningless.
3
Apply the same logic to yad (hand)
Notice the identical structure: rejecting literalism (physical hand) and figurative interpretation (power). The key is the specification of Adam's creation.
The Shaykh's reasoning is consistent across attributes.
4
Observe the pattern for ʿayn and wajh
Even though the passage cuts off, the same method is implied. See how the verses quoted (e.g., 'under My eye') follow the same logic of specification.
5
Reflect on the principle of specification
The core argument: if the attribute referred only to God's omnipotence, then the specific mention of the Throne or Adam's creation would be pointless. Therefore, the attribute must be a real, unique divine attribute.
This principle is central to Ash'ari methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دليل من أثبت الصفات السمعية غير الثمانية المتقدمة مع نفي ظواهرها وأما الشيخ فاعتمد في إثبات هذه الصفات على ظواهرها من القرآن : فأما ( الاستواء ) : فاحتج على ثبوته بقوله تعالى : ﴿ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ استوى ﴾ [طـه : ٥] فقال : الاستواء بمعنى الاستقرار والتمكن بالجلوس.. مستحيل عقلا وإجماعا ، وتأويله بالاستيلاء على العرش بالقدرة يوجب ألا يكون لتخصيص العرش بذلك فائدة ؛ إذ سائر الممكنات تماثل العرش في ذلك ، فوجب أن يحمل الاستواء على صفة تليق به جل وعز ، والله تعالى أعلم بحقيقتها . ودليله على الصفة التي تسمى بـ ( اليد ) : قوله تعالى لإبليس : ﴿ مَا مَنَعَكَ أَن تَسْجُدَ لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَى ﴾ [ص : ٧٥] قال : ولا وجه لحمل اليدين على القدرة ؛ إذ جملة المبتدعات مخترعة بالقدرة ، ففي الحمل على ذلك إبطال فائدة التخصيص ودليله على إثبات الصفة التي تسمى بـ ( العين ) : قوله تعالى : ﴿ وَلِتُصْنَعَ عَلَى عَيْنِي ﴾ [طه : ٣٩] . ودليله على الصفة التي تسمى بـ ( الوجه ) : قوله تعالى :
The proof of those who affirmed the auditory attributes beyond the eight [essential attributes] while negating their apparent meanings. As for the Shaykh, he relied in affirming these attributes on their apparent meanings from the Qur'an. As for al-istiwā' (the establishing), he argued for its affirmation by His saying, Most High: 'He established Himself over the Throne' [Taha:5]. He said: al-istiwā' in the sense of settling and being firmly seated is impossible by reason and consensus, and interpreting it as domination (al-istīlā') over the Throne by power necessitates that there be no benefit in specifying the Throne thereby, since all other possible things resemble the Throne in that, so it is necessary that al-istiwā' be interpreted as an attribute befitting Him, Mighty and Majestic, and Allah Most High knows its true reality. And his proof for the attribute called 'al-yad' (hand) is His saying to Iblīs: 'What prevented you from prostrating to what I created with My two hands' [Sad:75]. He said: There is no way to interpret the two hands as power, since all created things are created by power, so interpreting them as such would nullify the benefit of specification. And his proof for affirming the attribute called 'al-ʿayn' (eye) is His saying: 'That you might be formed under My eye' [Taha:39]. And his proof for the attribute called 'al-wajh' (face) is His saying:
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage first presents the proof of those who negate the apparent meanings of the auditory attributes, though it immediately states that the Shaykh (al-Ashʿari) actually relies on the apparent meanings. The author then gives the Shaykh's arguments for four specific attributes: al-istiwā', al-yad, al-ʿayn, and al-wajh. For al-istiwā', the Shaykh argues that the apparent meaning (settling) is impossible for God, but interpreting it as mere domination (istīlā') would make the specification of the Throne meaningless because God dominates everything. Therefore, it must be an attribute unique to God. For al-yad, similar reasoning: interpreting 'hands' as power would not specify Adam's creation, since all creation is by power. So 'hands' must be a real attribute. For al-ʿayn, the verse from Taha is cited. The passage ends mid-sentence for al-wajh, but the pattern suggests a similar argument.

Misconception: The Shaykh accepts the literal, anthropomorphic meaning of attributes like 'hand' and 'eye'.
Correction: The Shaykh rejects the literal meaning (e.g., physical hand) but also rejects purely figurative interpretation. He affirms a real attribute whose true nature is known only to God.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

Proof for the Attribute of al-Istiwā' from Its Apparent Meaning
Sanusi presents al-Shaykh's proof for istiwā' and refutes ta'wīl as istīlā'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Shaykh's argument for affirming the attribute of istiwā' based on its apparent Quranic meaning and his refutation of interpreting it as domination.

Core Idea
Affirming istiwā' as a real attribute requires rejecting both its literal physical meaning and its ta'wīl as domination.

Sanusi now presents al-Shaykh's approach to the transmitted attributes that go beyond the eight essential attributes. For istiwā', al-Shaykh uses the verse 'The Most Gracious rose over the Throne' to argue that the attribute must be affirmed in a way befitting Allah, rejecting both anthropomorphism and the common reinterpretation as domination. This passage is key to understanding the Ash'ari method of handling ambiguous verses.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the literal translation. Note the structure: first a general statement about al-Shaykh's method, then the specific argument for istiwā'.
Pay attention to the verse citation and the logical flow.
2
Identify the two rejections
Al-Shaykh rejects two interpretations: the literal meaning (sitting) as impossible, and the ta'wīl as domination as pointless. Identify why each is rejected.
The first rejection is by reason and consensus; the second is by necessity.
3
Grasp the conclusion
The conclusion is that istiwā' must be an attribute specific to Allah, the true nature of which is known only to Him. This is the principle of tafwīd.
This conclusion protects against both anthropomorphism and negation of attributes.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دليلُ مَنْ أثبت الصفاتِ السمعية غير الثمانية المتقدمة مع نفي ظواهرها وأمَّا الشيخ فاعتمد في إثباتِ هذه الصفاتِ على ظواهرها مِنَ القرآن: أمَّا ( الاستواء ) : فاحتج على ثبوتِهِ بقولِهِ تعالى : ﴿ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى [طـه : ٥] فقال: الاستواء بمعنى الاستقرار والتمكُنِ بالجلوس.. مستحيل عقلاً وإجماعاً، وتأويله بالاستيلاء على العرش بالقدرة يُوجِبُ ألا يكونَ لتخصيص العرش بذلك فائدةٌ؛ إذْ سائر الممكناتِ تماثل العرش في ذلكَ، فوجبَ أَنْ يُحمل الاستواء على صفةٍ تليقُ بهِ جلَّ وعزَّ، والله تعالى أعلم بحقيقتها.
The proof of one who affirms the transmitted attributes other than the eight previously mentioned while negating their apparent meanings. As for al-Shaykh, he relied in establishing these attributes on their apparent meanings from the Quran. As for al-istiwā': he argued for its affirmation by His statement, the Most High: {The Most Gracious rose over the Throne} [Taha: 5]. He said: al-istiwā' in the sense of settling and firmly planting oneself by sitting is impossible by reason and consensus. And its interpretation as domination over the Throne by power necessitates that there be no benefit in specifying the Throne thereby, since all [other] possible things resemble the Throne in that. So it is necessary that al-istiwā' be carried upon an attribute befitting Him, the Mighty and Majestic, and Allah knows best its true reality.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage presents the proof for the attribute of al-istiwā' as understood by al-Shaykh, who adheres to the apparent meanings of the Quranic verses. It begins by contrasting his approach with those who negate the apparent meanings. The passage focuses on the verse {al-Rahman istawā 'alā al-'arsh}. Al-Shaykh argues that interpreting istiwā' literally as physical sitting is impossible both rationally and by consensus. He then critiques the common ta'wīl of istiwā' as istīlā' (domination), stating that if it meant domination, then specifying the Throne would have no special benefit, because all created things are under Allah's domination equally. Therefore, the only valid conclusion is that istiwā' must be an attribute specific to Allah, whose true nature is known only to Allah. The passage ends by affirming the principle of tafwīd (consigning the modality to Allah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that rejecting the apparent meaning of istiwā' necessarily leads to anthropomorphism.
Correction: The passage shows that the correct approach is to affirm an attribute befitting Allah without likening to creation, rejecting both literal interpretation and figurative interpretation.

Checkpoint
What is the main argument against interpreting 'istawā' as 'istīlā' (domination)?
A) It is rationally impossible.
B) It contradicts consensus.
C) It would make the specification of the Throne pointless.
D) It implies sitting.

Key Takeaway
Al-Shaykh affirms istiwā' as a real attribute of Allah, rejecting both anthropomorphism and figurative interpretation, and consigning its true nature to Allah alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verse 'al-Rahmānu ʿalā l-ʿarshi istawā', do you feel a tension between your mind's desire to understand and your heart's duty to submit? Are you willing to affirm what Allah affirms without fully grasping it, or do you find yourself drawn to explanations that make the attribute more 'reasonable' to your intellect?
?
This passage shows that the ta'wīl of istiwā' as domination leads to a logical inconsistency. But more urgently, what does your soul say about Allah's nearness? Are you content to say 'Allāh knows best its reality' and let that be enough, or do you secretly crave a tangible image to cling to? What does that craving reveal about the state of your tawḥīd?
?
Consider your own inclinations: when faced with a divine attribute that confounds human logic, do you rush to reinterpret it to fit your mind, or do you humbly consign its true nature to Allah? What does your response reveal about your heart's posture towards Allah's words and your willingness to worship Him as He is, not as you imagine Him to be?
